## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science & solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most commonly arise in constitutive laws for solids (elasticity/plasticity/viscoelasticity) with temperature-dependent stiffness, yield/flow stress, and thermal strain effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke’s law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain, linear elastic regime)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear thermoelastic stiffness): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (E varies approximately linearly with T)
- Polynomial E(T) (higher-order stiffness variation): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (fitting modulus over a wider T range)
- Exponential softening of modulus with temperature: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (captures rapid stiffening/softening vs T; c1 often negative for softening)
- Thermal strain (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (constrained thermal expansion/shrinkage)
- Thermoelastic with E(T) and thermal strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (common engineering thermoelastic form)
- Nonlinear (second-order) elasticity with temperature-dependent coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (moderate strain nonlinearity + thermal effect)
- Exponential strain-hardening (hyperelastic-like stiffening): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (large-strain stiffening with temperature scaling)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (captures work hardening in epsilon and monotone T effect)
- Johnson–Cook-like (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)**c5 (plastic flow stress with strain hardening and temperature dependence)
- Smooth yield/transition with temperature (glass transition / phase softening proxy): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (c2 + exp(c3 * (T - c4))) (effective strength drops across a characteristic T)
- Entropic/rubber-like elasticity scaling with temperature: sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) (stress roughly proportional to absolute temperature in entropic elasticity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion under constraint often appears as an offset in strain: replace epsilon by (epsilon - c * (T - T0)) to model stress-free thermal strain.
- Elastic modulus typically decreases with temperature in metals/polymers: use E(T) multiplying epsilon where E(T) is linear/polynomial or exp(c*T) with negative c.
- Plastic/flow stress commonly shows separable structure: sigma ≈ g(epsilon) * h(T), where g hardens with epsilon and h softens with T.
- Glass-transition or phase-change softening vs T is often captured by a smooth step in T (e.g., logistic/tanh-like denominators) multiplying an otherwise strain-driven stress.
- Large-strain stiffening (polymer networks, some hyperelastic responses) is better captured by exp(c*epsilon) or rapidly increasing functions than by low-order polynomials.
- Tension–compression asymmetry or sign-sensitivity (if present in data) can be represented by using epsilon and Abs(epsilon) in combination (odd/even decomposition).
- Near-linear elastic behavior at small strain but nonlinear at larger strain suggests additive terms: sigma = E(T)*epsilon + K(T)*epsilon**n (n>1) rather than a single power law.
- If sigma tends to zero at high T for fixed epsilon (thermal weakening), structures with exp(c*T) (c<0) or reciprocal-in-T transitions are physically plausible.

GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) + c4*epsilon**c5 + c6*(T - c7)*sin(epsilon)
Candidates evaluated: 58

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `99.72829794207104*epsilon*(-0.08976441603442807*(T - 330.599841780566) + 1) + 4.818532892851478*epsilon**3 + 5.41673901332906*(T - 330.599841780566)*sin(epsilon)`

Let me expand the GT:
- First term: `99.728*epsilon*(1 - 0.08976*(T - 330.6))` = `99.728*epsilon - 99.728*0.08976*epsilon*(T-330.6)` = `99.728*epsilon - 8.952*epsilon*T + 8.952*330.6*epsilon`
- Simplifying: `99.728*epsilon - 8.952*epsilon*T + 2960.1*epsilon` = `(99.728 + 2960.1)*epsilon - 8.952*T*epsilon`

Wait, let me be more careful:
- `99.728*epsilon*(1 - 0.08976*T + 0.08976*330.6)` = `99.728*epsilon*(1 + 29.674 - 0.08976*T)` = `99.728*epsilon*(30.674 - 0.08976*T)`

So GT = `99.728*(30.674 - 0.08976*T)*epsilon + 4.8185*epsilon**3 + 5.4167*(T - 330.6)*sin(epsilon)`

The GT has these basis function components:
1. **epsilon** (linear in epsilon)
2. **T*epsilon** (product of T and epsilon)
3. **epsilon**3** (cubic in epsilon)
4. **T*sin(epsilon)** (product of T and sin(epsilon))
5. **sin(epsilon)** (just sin(epsilon))

So GT = A*epsilon + B*T*epsilon + C*epsilon³ + D*T*sin(epsilon) + E*sin(epsilon)

where A, B, C, D, E are specific constants.

Now I need to check each candidate for the ability to produce these exact basis functions. The key basis functions needed are: {epsilon, T*epsilon, epsilon³, T*sin(epsilon), sin(epsilon)}.

Let me systematically check candidates that have T-dependent terms and sin/epsilon terms:

**Candidate 2:** `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + T*c3*epsilon + T*c4 + c5*exp(c6*epsilon) + c7 + c8*epsilon`

This has: T*sin(c1*epsilon+c2), T*epsilon, T, exp(c6*epsilon), constant, epsilon.
- GT needs T*sin(epsilon): set c1=1, c2=0 → T*c0*sin(epsilon) ✓
- GT needs T*epsilon: T*c3*epsilon ✓
- GT needs epsilon³: would need exp(c6*epsilon) to equal epsilon³, which is impossible ✗

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*sin(c3*epsilon + c4) + c5 + c6*exp(c7*sin(c8*epsilon + c9))`
Has: T*epsilon, epsilon, sin, constant, exp(sin(...))
Missing: T*sin(epsilon), epsilon³
Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 17:** `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**c3 + c4 + c5*exp(c6*sin(c7*epsilon + c8))`
Has: T*epsilon, epsilon, epsilon^c3 (can be epsilon³), constant, exp(c6*sin(...))
Missing: T*sin(epsilon). The exp(sin) term cannot produce T*sin(epsilon).
Candidate 17 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Let me check candidates with both T*sin(epsilon) and epsilon³ or equivalent:

Missing epsilon³.

**Candidate 14:** `T*c0*sin(c1*epsilon + c2) + T*c3*exp(c4*epsilon) + T*c5 + c6*epsilon + c7 + c8*epsilon`
Same issue - no epsilon³.
Candidate 14 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Most candidates lack T*sin(epsilon) or T*epsilon or epsilon³. Let me focus on candidates that might have all needed terms.

**Candidate 25:** `T*c0*epsilon**2 + T*c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*exp(c4*sin(c5*epsilon+c6)) + c7*log(c8*exp(c9*epsilon)+1) + epsilon`
Has T*epsilon² instead of T*sin(epsilon). No match.
Candidate 25 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 37:** `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1*epsilon**2 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*exp(c5*sin(c6*epsilon+c7)) + c8*epsilon**2`
Missing T*sin(epsilon).
Candidate 37 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 45:** `T*c0*epsilon**2 + c1*epsilon + c2 + c3*exp(c4*sin(c5*epsilon+c6)) + c7*epsilon**2`
Missing T*sin(epsilon), T*epsilon, epsilon³.
Candidate 45 verdict: [NO MATCH]

After careful analysis, none of the candidates contain the required combination of T*sin(epsilon) AND epsilon³ (or equivalent). Most candidates either lack T-dependence entirely, or have T only linearly (not multiplied by sin(epsilon)), or lack the polynomial epsilon³ term.
